# Notes: Ashlr Autonomous Fleet Ambition Push

## Current Dispatch Manifest Status
- Context: the previous commit began recording metadata-only concurrent dispatch manifests before `runConcurrentDispatch()`. The follow-up gap was operator visibility: the ledger existed, but `FleetStatus` and CLI output could not yet answer "what concurrent plan did the daemon intend to run?"
- Implementation: `FleetStatus.dispatchManifests` now reads the append-only manifest ledger fail-soft, bounded to recent events, and aggregates event count, latest timestamp, assigned/unassigned totals, backend assignment counts, and a bounded recent sample. `ashlr fleet status` renders the same manifest summary under Dispatch yield.
- Safety boundary: this is read-only forensic observability, not a queue, lease, retry source, or merge gate. The surface uses manifest ids, timestamps, counts, backend names, and bounded metadata only; it does not persist or render raw prompts, diffs, stdout, stderr, env, file contents, command output, or secrets.
- Verification passed: focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts test/m353.dispatch-manifest.test.ts` (70 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `git diff --check`, `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`, `npm run lint` (known 114-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, and `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`.
- Sibling verifier progress: `webfetch` now has a pushed `ashlr.verify.json` on `codex/webfetch-verify-manifest` after `bun run typecheck` and `bun test` passed. `stack` now has a pushed `ashlr.verify.json` on `codex/stack-verify-manifest` after `bun run typecheck`, `bun test`, `bun run build`, CLI smokes, and Hub profile detection passed. Both workers left pre-existing dirty/unrelated work untouched.

## Current Prompt-Trackr Merge Contract
- Selection: verifier scout ranked `prompt-trackr` as the safest next explicit contract because its branch `codex/prompt-trackr-agent-docs` was synced to `origin`, had a real remote, and only one pre-existing dirty tracked test file. `ashlrcode` and `ashlr-plugin` are better handled after dirty WIP is isolated.
- Implementation: added root `ashlr.verify.json` in `/Users/masonwyatt/Desktop/github/dev-tools/prompt-trackr` with `mode:"replace-detected"` and required merge-profile commands for `npm run typecheck`, `npm run build`, and `npm run test`.
- Validation: Hub profile detection reports `mergeGradeExplicit:true` with 3 required merge-profile commands. `npm run typecheck`, `npm run build`, and `npm run test` passed. `npm run lint` is intentionally not a required merge gate yet because the repo currently has a pre-existing lint backlog (`40` errors, `162` warnings) unrelated to the manifest.
- Push: committed `d9fade5 chore: Add Ashlr verification contract` and pushed it to `origin/codex/prompt-trackr-agent-docs`. The pre-existing dirty file `src/app/api/__tests__/leaderboard-composite.test.ts` remained unstaged.
- Fleet coverage: after `bin/ashlr backlog refresh --json`, FleetStatus moved to `14/24` explicit merge contracts, with 10 repos still missing explicit contracts. Remaining missing names: `ashlr sales pipeline`, `ashlr-core-efficiency`, `ashlr-md`, `ashlr-plugin`, `ashlr-workbench`, `ashlrcode`, `morphkit`, `phantom-secrets`, `stack`, and `webfetch`.
- Follow-up risk: GitHub reported 3 default-branch Dependabot vulnerabilities for `prompt-trackr` during push. That is a separate security lane from the verifier manifest.

## Current Selection Workspace Telemetry
- Research input: recent multi-agent and long-running-agent guidance converges on durable session/workspace logs, end-state checkpoints, artifact handoffs, and explicit monitoring. The Hub already had append-only action telemetry; the gap was that queue selection and non-dispatch skips were not fully broadcast into that workspace.
- Implementation: daemon ticks now emit a metadata-only `daemon:selection` agent-action row after final selection/claim, with backlog, eligible, pending-blocked, cooldown-blocked, fast-repair-cooldown, selected, and claimed counts. This records why the fleet attended to a lane before any dispatch happens.
- Generated repair decisions: trusted generated repair items now emit bounded item-level `daemon:generated-repair-decision` rows, capped per tick, with enum reasons such as `claimed`, `pending-proposal`, `cooldown: latest=empty`, `cooldown: latest=judged-decline`, `claim-missed`, or `not-selected`. Counts include base/effective cooldown, fast-repair flag, pending/cooldown blockers, selected, and claimed.
- Dispatch skips: selected items skipped before engine invocation now emit `daemon:dispatch-skip` rows with repo/item id, route metadata, backend/tier/model when known, and skip reason. These rows intentionally do not enter dispatch-production yield denominators, because a budget/resource/kill-switch skip is not a proposal-production attempt.
- Privacy boundary: no prompts, diffs, stdout, stderr, env, argv, file contents, or `WorkItem.detail` are persisted. The new rows use bounded ids, enum-like reasons, numeric counts, fixed tags, and existing causal metadata only.
- Verification passed: `npm run test:ci -- test/m201.daemon-loop.test.ts` (93 tests), `npm run test:ci -- test/m343.agent-action-ledger.test.ts test/m349.secret-safety-invariants.test.ts test/m352.attempt-records.test.ts` (36 tests), and `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`.
- Next implication: Ashlr can now reconstruct not only which generated repair converted, but also which repair was cooled, pending-blocked, selected, claimed, or skipped by budget/resource policy. This is the decision substrate needed for a real recursive learning loop.

## Current Repair Recovery Fast Cooldown And UI
- Start state: generated repair recovery was measurable and healthy (`4/5` generated repair attempts converted, `80%`), but trusted repair items that returned empty diffs still waited behind the generic six-hour worked-ledger cooldown. Fleet OS also lacked a first-class repair-loop metric, so operators could not see that the loop was actively recovering.
- Implementation: daemon selection and read-only FleetStatus queue eligibility now use a repair-aware cooldown only when generated repair recovery is healthy and the latest worked event for a trusted generated repair item is `empty`. The fast cooldown is capped at 30 minutes; judged review/noise/decline outcomes keep the full cooldown.
- Trust boundary: the fast lane is limited to `isTrustedGeneratedRepairItem()`, which combines the existing strict generated no-diff reslice and capture-repair predicates. It does not weaken pending-proposal dedupe, enrollment checks, budget/resource gates, sandboxing, merge authority, branch protection, or evidence requirements.
- Fleet OS visibility: Mission Control, Fleet Dashboard readiness, and dispatch-production panels now surface aggregate `Repair Loop` / `Repair recovery` metrics from metadata-only generated repair counts. The repair-loop UI uses counts, rates, and fixed repair-kind labels only; it does not render prompts, diffs, stdout/stderr, command output, file contents, repo paths, or item IDs.
- Verification passed: adjacent `npm run test:ci -- test/m310.queued-autonomy-work.test.ts test/m342.dispatch-production-ledger.test.ts test/m352.attempt-records.test.ts` (46 tests), focused repair/status/dashboard coverage `npm run test:ci -- test/m201.daemon-loop.test.ts test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts test/m210.dashboard.test.ts test/m213.dashboard-sse.test.ts` (202 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`, `git diff --check`, plus previously run `npm run lint`, `npm run build`, and `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`.
- Production push: pushed `c128c70 feat: Fast-track healthy repair recovery` to `origin/master`.
- Live smoke after reload: launchd daemon PID `98537`, guard clear, no pending proposals, and FleetStatus now places `ashlr-hub:proposal-repair-capture:77ea0de4dbbd` first in `queue.next`. The diagnostic reslice drain also shows `available:5`, `selected:1`, `automatic:true`, and `proposalsCreated:1`, proving the repair fast lane is actively converting in production.
- Next implication: the fleet can now retry high-yield generated repair work faster when the prior failure was only an empty diff, without rerunning manager-rejected work. The next highest-leverage lanes are causal skip/selection telemetry and Fleet OS source/data-quality controls.

## Current Active Repair Recovery Status
- Start state: after generated repair yield telemetry landed, FleetStatus showed `5` generated repair attempts with `4` proposals created (`80%` conversion), but Autonomous Ship Readiness still used the generic `dispatch-yield-actionable` blocker for the broader local-coder/self historical sample.
- Scout finding: the smallest safe next step was status/action intelligence, not a new daemon drain mode. Use aggregate repair conversion to distinguish "recovery is working" from "yield is simply bad," while requiring enough samples and active generated repair work so the signal cannot hide weak evidence.
- Implementation: dispatch-yield diagnostics now carry `generatedRepairAttempts`, action/readiness details include `repair recovery: generated repairs ...`, and `generatedRepairRecoveryStatus()` treats recovery as healthy only when generated repair work is active, has at least three attempts, and converts at or above `max(configured low-yield floor, 50%)`.
- Readiness behavior: when dispatch yield remains actionable but generated repair recovery is healthy, readiness now reports low-severity `generated-repair-recovery-active` instead of medium `dispatch-yield-actionable`. The underlying diagnostic candidate, attempt shape, queued repair coverage, and conversion counts remain visible.
- Action behavior: generic `inspect-dispatch-yield` is suppressed only when a concrete repair monitor action is active. If no repair item is currently daemon-eligible, the generic inspect action remains visible so the fleet does not overstate progress.
- Verification passed: focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts` (63 tests), adjacent `npm run test:ci -- test/m342.dispatch-production-ledger.test.ts test/m352.attempt-records.test.ts test/m213.dashboard-sse.test.ts test/m210.dashboard.test.ts test/m201.daemon-loop.test.ts test/m46.fleet.test.ts` (191 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `npm run lint` (known 114-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`, and `git diff --check`.
- Production push/reload: pushed `ee87b95 feat: Surface active repair recovery` to `origin/master`, reinstalled/kickstarted launchd, and smoked daemon PID `34126` with guard clear.
- Live post-deploy signal: readiness top blocker is now `generated-repair-recovery-active` with detail `generated repairs 4/5 converted (80%; capture 2, no-diff 3)`. Primary action remains `resource-claude` because Claude is constrained. `inspect-dispatch-yield` remains visible because current `queue.next` is generic goal/Phantom work rather than an eligible repair item, suggesting the next Hub lane is repair-aware queue selection or broader generated-repair drain once the fleet proves repair items are being starved.

## Current Generated Repair Yield Telemetry
- Start state: generated repair items were visible in the queue and now route better, but production learning only showed generic no-diff/gate shapes plus runtime verification repair attempts. The fleet could not answer the critical recursive-learning question: do generated repair items actually convert into proposals?
- Scout finding: use a fixed metadata-only enum, not raw item titles or free-text reasons. Deterministic generated item ids and known generated title prefixes are enough to bucket `capture-repair`, `no-diff-reslice`, and `proposal-repair` attempts.
- Implementation: `generatedRepairAttemptKindFromSignals()` classifies generated repair work from `itemId`/`title` metadata, `productionAttemptShapeFromSignals()` counts generated repair work as `repairAttempts`, and dispatch-production plus attempt-coverage summaries now expose generated repair attempts, proposal/no-proposal counts, proposal rate, and per-kind counts.
- CLI/status: `ashlr fleet status` renders compact repair-yield lines under Dispatch yield and Attempt coverage, e.g. `capture 1 attempt, no-diff 1 attempt; 1/2 converted (50%)`.
- Privacy boundary: learning labels and summaries persist only fixed counters/rates and bounded attempt shapes. Tests assert raw generated titles are not stored in labels or aggregate repair summaries; prompts, diffs, stdout, stderr, env, argv, and file contents remain out of learning ledgers.
- Verification passed: focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m342.dispatch-production-ledger.test.ts test/m352.attempt-records.test.ts test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts` (97 tests), adjacent `npm run test:ci -- test/m201.daemon-loop.test.ts test/m250.resource-control.test.ts test/m46.fleet.test.ts test/m310.queued-autonomy-work.test.ts` (164 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `npm run lint` (known 114-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`, and `git diff --check`.
- Production push/reload: pushed `46b404e feat: Track generated repair yield` to `origin/master`, reinstalled/kickstarted launchd, archived stale spend guard from old PID `14293`, resumed the fleet after the stop command engaged the kill switch, and smoked daemon PID `87275` with guard clear.
- Live signal after deploy: FleetStatus reports generated repair attempts in both `dispatchProduction` and `attemptCoverage.production`: `5` attempts, `4` proposals created, `1` no-proposal, `80%` proposal rate, `2` capture repairs, `3` no-diff reslices, and `0` proposal repairs. Readiness is still degraded by dispatch yield because the wider historical window remains weak, but the repair lane itself is now measurable and currently high-yield.
- Next implication: the fleet can now learn from generated repair work without a judge. The next high-leverage lane is either to close the remaining dispatch-yield blocker by making generated repair work more aggressively selected under resource constraints, or to repair Phantom's merge-grade verifier blocker once its dirty WIP/clippy state can be isolated safely.

## Current Protected Capture Repair Routing
- Start state: after the policy-suppressed label fix, live FleetStatus still had readiness degraded by `dispatch-yield-actionable`, primary action `process-capture-repairs`, 7 generated proposal-repair items, and 2 eligible capture repairs. Claude was exhausted, while Codex/NIM/Kimi were open, so repair routing needed to preserve frontier intent but remain resource-aware.
- Scout consensus: no-diff diagnostic reslices already had a strict generated-shape trust predicate and frontier route reason. Generated capture repairs needed the same narrow escape hatch so repair work would not be routed back through the weak local/self path that produced the capture failure.
- Implementation: added `isTrustedCaptureRepairItem()` with deterministic `:proposal-repair-capture:<12hex>` id, generated tags, generated detail markers, and either diff metadata or actionable failure text. `routeBackend()` now treats trusted capture repairs as frontier candidates and emits `frontier: generated capture proposal repair`.
- Safety hardening: self-heal trust helpers now treat missing/non-array tags as empty, so sanitized or malformed queue samples fail closed instead of throwing. Tag-only/manual lookalikes and samples without tags are not promoted.
- Resource/dispatch behavior: workhorse dispatch already preserves `frontier:` hints; new coverage proves generated capture-repair frontier hints do not spread to `local-coder`. Resource-aware gateway coverage proves an exhausted selected frontier demotes to an open frontier alternative rather than falling straight to local workhorse capacity.
- Verification passed: focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m46.fleet.test.ts test/m250.resource-control.test.ts test/m256.workhorse-dispatch.test.ts test/m310.queued-autonomy-work.test.ts` (88 tests), adjacent `npm run test:ci -- test/m201.daemon-loop.test.ts test/m255.concurrent-dispatch.test.ts test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts` (180 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `npm run lint` (known 114-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`, and `git diff --check`.
- Production push/reload: pushed `e255c05 feat: Route capture repairs through frontier`, reinstalled/kickstarted launchd, and live smoke showed daemon PID `14293`, guard clear, active tick, `$0.087228` spent today, readiness still degraded by dispatch yield, primary action `process-capture-repairs`, and one visible `ashlrcode` capture repair remaining while the prior top `ashlr-hub` capture repair had moved off the front of `queue.next`.

## Current Policy-Suppressed Label Weak Gate
- Start state: live FleetStatus had `causalCoverage.currentAuthoritativeLabel` at `14/38`, but the remaining current-label gaps were policy-suppressed attempts rather than learnable production attempts. That created an `inspect-attempt-causal-coverage` style weak signal even though `causalGapDiagnostics.actionableCauses` was empty.
- Implementation: `summarizeAttemptCoverage()` now evaluates the `currentAuthoritativeLabel` weak gate against non-policy-suppressed records only, while preserving the raw all-attempt `causalCoverage.currentAuthoritativeLabel` count/rate for transparency. Policy-suppressed rows still appear in causal diagnostics and blocked-current-label counts.
- Status polish: weak reasons can carry an explicit denominator, and `FleetStatus` next-action detail uses it so learnable-only weak metrics do not display against total attempts.
- Regression coverage: `m352` now proves one learnable current label plus two policy-suppressed unlabeled attempts keeps `causalWeak.weak:false` while diagnostics still report the two policy-suppressed blocked labels.
- Verification passed: focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m352.attempt-records.test.ts test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts test/m213.dashboard-sse.test.ts` (100 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `git diff --check`, final `npm run lint` (known 114-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, and `node --check src/core/web/public/app.js`.

## Current Diagnostic No-Diff Reslice Queue
- Start state: clean pushed `master` at `04c366f`; daemon PID `64076`, guard clear, queue `33` backlog / `31` eligible / `0` pending, readiness degraded by `dispatch-yield-actionable`, and autonomy effectiveness `proposal-starved`.
- Agent pool was saturated for a new explorer wave, so implementation proceeded locally using prior scout findings plus direct audit of `proposal-repair-work`, queued autonomy, self-heal trust, daemon producer maintenance, and existing m310/m201 regressions.
- Implementation: proposal repair maintenance now scans recent dispatch-production `empty-diff` rows and writes metadata-only `diagnostic-reslice` self-heal items with stable `proposal-repair-nodiff` ids. Items include original item id, source, backend, route reason, outcome, sanitized reason, and an action to reslice with retrieved context; they do not persist raw prompts, diffs, stdout, stderr, env, or file contents.
- Safety/trust: `isActionableSelfHealItem()` has a narrow explicit path for generated `proposal-repair + diagnostic-reslice + dispatch-no-diff-reslice` items, requiring expected detail markers plus the deterministic `:proposal-repair-nodiff:<hash>` id shape. The first focused run caught an over-strict colon word-boundary regex; fixed by matching the markers without requiring a word boundary after `:`.
- Daemon telemetry: `producerMaintenance` now exposes `dispatchNoDiffResliceScanned/Eligible/Queued/Failed` alongside proposal and capture-gate repair counts.
- Verification passed: `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `git diff --check`, focused `m310/m201/m49/m342/m346/m349` before hardening (162 tests), adjacent `m165/m352/m343/m255/m256` (113 tests), full `npm run test:ci` before final hardening (439 files, 9,090 passed, 7 skipped), focused `m310/m201/m49/m342/m346/m349` after hardening (163 tests), `npm run test:invariants` (41 files, 411 tests), final `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `npm run lint` (existing 115-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate` (0 vulnerabilities), and `git diff --check`.
- Production push/reload: pushed `4269726 feat: Queue no-diff diagnostic reslices`, reinstalled and kickstarted launchd, released the kill switch with `bin/ashlr fleet resume`, and live smoke showed daemon PID `83207`, guard clear, queue `33` backlog / `31` eligible / `0` pending / `2` cooldown, 24/24 enrolled repos with backlog, 21 missing explicit merge contracts, resources `builtin/open`, `local-coder/open`, `claude/open`, `codex/open`, `nim/open`, `kimi/open`, and readiness still degraded by `dispatch-yield-actionable` / `proposal-starved`.

## Current Explicit Merge Contract Wave 3
- Homebrew detector bug: Hub was emitting `brew audit --strict --formula Formula/*.rb`, but current Homebrew refuses path arguments (`Calling brew audit [path ...] is disabled`) and name/tap audit can fail on untrusted taps. The safe inferred Homebrew verifier is now deterministic Ruby syntax checking (`ruby -c Formula/*.rb`); stronger audit commands should be explicit, opt-in, and trust-aware.
- Implementation: updated `homebrewFormulaProject()` and `m314` coverage so Homebrew detection no longer emits trust/path-sensitive audit commands.
- Manifests: added root `ashlr.verify.json` to `homebrew-ashlr` (three `ruby -c` formula checks), `homebrew-phantom` (one `ruby -c` formula check), and `openclaw-setup` (`python -m pytest -q`).

## Current Frontier Route No-Diff Reslices
- Live bottleneck: FleetStatus is still proposal-starved with `28/30` eligible backlog items, no pending proposals, and five generated diagnostic no-diff reslices queued. Those reslices had `source:"self"` and modest scores, so the router could treat them as `local-mid bulk` and send them back to the same low-yield local path.
- Implementation: `routeBackend()` now treats items tagged with both `proposal-repair` and `dispatch-no-diff-reslice` as frontier candidates when a frontier backend is allowed and installed. The route reason starts with `frontier:` so workhorse dispatch preserves the protected route instead of spreading it back to local bulk lanes.
- Compatibility: if no frontier backend is available, existing mid/builtin fallback behavior remains unchanged. Ordinary self-heal or proposal-repair items without the diagnostic no-diff reslice tag are not promoted by this rule.
- Verification passed: `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`; focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m46.fleet.test.ts test/m255.concurrent-dispatch.test.ts test/m256.workhorse-dispatch.test.ts test/m250.resource-control.test.ts` (100 tests); `git diff --check`; `npm run lint` (known 115-warning baseline, 0 errors); `npm run build`; and `npm audit --audit-level=moderate` (0 vulnerabilities).

## Current Daemon Active Tick Freshness
- Live finding: after launchd kickstart, the daemon process owned a fresh singleton lock and launchd stderr showed active engine runs, but `FleetStatus.daemon.lastTickAt` stayed stale because it only records completed ticks. Autonomous Ship Readiness therefore marked the daemon source stale during productive long-running ticks.
- Implementation: FleetStatus now carries additive daemon fields: `startedAt`, `lockHeartbeatAt`, and `tickInProgress`. The readiness daemon source uses a matching live lock heartbeat as the observed freshness timestamp and explains when a tick is in progress, while preserving the last completed tick timestamp.
- CLI: `ashlr fleet status` now prints daemon started time, active tick state, and heartbeat when available.
- Verification passed: `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`; focused `npm run test:ci -- test/m49.fleet-status.test.ts test/m61.control.test.ts test/m210.dashboard.test.ts` (100 tests); `git diff --check`; `npm run lint` (known 115-warning baseline, 0 errors); `npm run build`; and `npm audit --audit-level=moderate` (0 vulnerabilities).
- Deployed as `13a6049` on `origin/master`, reinstalled/resumed/kickstarted launchd, and re-smoked live status. Settled JSON showed daemon `running:true`, fresh `lockHeartbeatAt`, `tickInProgress:true`, daemon readiness source `healthy/fresh`, and overall readiness freshness `fresh` while mission remained `Recover dispatch yield`.

## Current Resource-Aware Learned Target Gate
- Start state: dirty Hub WIP after comparative learned routing rollout; Entire remains not set up for `master`.
- Implementation: `recommendRoute()` now accepts optional metadata-only `resourceStates` and filters comparative same-tier learned reroute candidates to `open` or `near` availability when provided. Missing candidates are blocked only in explicit resource-aware calls; direct/legacy learned-router callers without `resourceStates` preserve previous behavior.
- Gateway integration: resource-aware `decide()` captures one resource snapshot before M53 and passes it to learned routing so learned target choice is based on the same capacity evidence as the initial route guard.
- Safety refinement from Popper scout: the final gateway resource demotion intentionally re-senses instead of reusing the initial snapshot, so a mid-decision `recordBackoff()` invalidation is observed before dispatch. This keeps learned routing efficient while preserving the final fail-safe.
- Regression coverage: `m53` covers open/near, throttled/exhausted/unreachable/unknown, and missing-snapshot learned target gates. `m250` covers gateway `m53Nudge` allowed/blocked traces and the mid-decision backoff re-sense path.

## Findings
- NVIDIA LocateAnything research follow-up: NVIDIA released LocateAnything-3B through NVlabs/Eagle and Hugging Face as a visual grounding model for GUI grounding, OCR/text localization, document layout, dense detection, and natural-language box/point localization. The project page highlights Parallel Box Decoding, 138M language queries, and 785M boxes. The repo code is Apache-2.0, but the Hugging Face model weights are NVIDIA-license non-commercial/research-use only, so Ashlr should not make it a default commercial dependency without license review.
- Visual grounding architecture decision: create a new `src/core/visual` namespace for pixel perception. Do not reuse `src/core/vision`, which stores the north-star/strategist vision system. The first patch should provide a safe provider abstraction, normalized box parser, explicit license/endpoint guards, and docs; MCP tools and browser/evidence-pack wiring can follow once the operator UX around screenshot upload is explicit.
- Reliability audit: biggest 24/7 risks are cross-process daemon singleton locking, fail-closed spend persistence, queue lease renewal for long frontier runs, hard enforcement of concurrent-dispatch backend assignments, fail-closed resource-control mode, and better fatal sidecar observability.
- Follow-up reliability patch: added a same-machine daemon singleton lock (`~/.ashlr/daemon.lock`) with token-checked release, heartbeat, dead-owner stale takeover, and `runDaemon` refusal before ticking when another process owns the lock.
- State persistence hardening: daemon saves now use unique temp files instead of one shared `daemon.json.tmp`, and `lastPulseExportAt` survives load/save cycles.
- Auto-merge effectiveness patch: Mission Control now surfaces successful `inbox:auto-merge` audit events, and auto-merge/inline merge judge signing now uses the shared GPT-5/Codex-aware frontier predicate instead of Claude-only checks.
- Quick reliability patch shipped: `restartSec` decouples OS service crash restart from daemon work interval. Default crash restart is 30s with a 5s minimum.
- Test/release audit: full serial Vitest can hang from leaked handles or long localhost/SSE probes. `test:ci` wrapper isolates HOME/ASHLR_HOME and kills the process group after a watchdog timeout.
- UX audit: Mission Control has strong telemetry but weak control surfaces. Inbox detail was reading `riskLevel` while proposals expose `riskClass`; patched to show risk, verification, and taste.
- Ecosystem audit: Hub overlaps with `@ashlr/config`, `@ashlr/cli-common`, `@ashlr/cost`, `@ashlr/mcp-kit`, `@ashlr/core-efficiency`, `ashlrcode`, `ashlr-plugin`, `phantom-secrets`, and `ashlr-pulse`. Next strategic lane is shared package adoption behind thin adapters.
- Security/dependency state: GitHub Dependabot alerts are Vite advisories through Vitest 2.x. `npm audit` recommends forced Vitest 4 upgrade; defer to focused migration.
- Shared queue hardening: long daemon dispatches now renew shared queue leases for the current machine, dry-runs release shared claims before returning, and atomic shared queue writes use unique temp files.
- Concurrent dispatch hardening: assigned resource-control backends now flow into actual execution instead of being rerouted inside the task closure; `throttled:`, `resource-pause:`, and `budget-pause:` decisions skip cleanly with audit coverage.
- CI isolation hardening: stale failures came from leaked `ASHLR_HOME`, fixed-date reflect seeds, learned-routing test contamination, and a stale secret-leak expectation around intentionally passed engine auth. The affected tests now isolate `ASHLR_HOME`, use relative dates, construct stable score fixtures, and allowlist engine auth passthrough only where intended.
- Operator control patch: Mission Control, Fleet, and Fleet Dashboard now include pause/resume controls backed by token-gated `/api/fleet/pause` and `/api/fleet/resume` endpoints. The endpoints stay hidden unless dispatch is enabled, preserve existing kill-switch semantics, and refresh fleet status after each action.
- Dependency security patch: upgraded from Vitest 2 to Vitest 3.2.6 and pinned Vite to 6.4.3 through `overrides`, clearing the Vite/esbuild advisory chain while avoiding the larger Vitest 4/Vite 8 migration.
- Plugin compatibility patch: Vitest 3's module runner can fail to import temporary external `.mjs` plugin entries from macOS `/var` paths, so the plugin registry now falls back to importing a base64 data URL for an existing entry file.
- Agent next lanes: spend persistence should fail closed on malformed or unwritable state; shared queue lease/reclaim health should be visible in Mission Control; daemon dispatches should expose backend assignment/reason traces; and the ecosystem needs a read-only `ashlr ecosystem doctor` inventory command.
- Spend persistence fail-closed patch: daemon state now has strict read/result-save APIs beside the forgiving dashboard APIs. `tick()` refuses before backlog/dispatch when `daemon.json` is malformed, when a spend guard is present, or when the normalized state cannot be saved before spend-capable work. Live ticks arm `daemon.spend-guard.json` before dispatch and only clear it after final spend accounting is strictly saved.
- Daemon loop hardening: `runDaemon()` now refuses start on strict state load/save failure, continuous/batch loop budget checks stop on strict load failure, and stop-state persistence audits failures instead of silently masking them.
- Queue health agent plan: add an additive `FleetStatus.queue.shared` object with active/expired/reclaimable leases, claims by machine, oldest expired age, next lease expiry, worked/cooldown/usage counts, and lock health; render in `/api/fleet`, `/api/control`, CLI fleet status, Mission Control, and Fleet Dashboard.
- Backend trace agent plan: gateway decisions already include reason/trace, but concurrent dispatch and daemon ticks collapse them to aggregates. Add `DaemonTick.dispatches` with item id/title/repo, assigned backend, reason, trace, and attempted/dispatched status; surface in Mission Control logs and Fleet Activity.
- Ecosystem doctor agent plan: add read-only `ashlr ecosystem doctor --json --root --deep` as an inventory command with synthetic sibling-repo tests, using existing `DoctorReport`/tool registry/dependency parser patterns without reusing write-capable doctor checks.
- Autonomy evidence pass: added `src/core/autonomy/evidence-pack.ts` and `src/core/autonomy/policy.ts` so autonomous actions produce a metadata-only evidence pack and a structured policy verdict (`T0` escalate through `T5` deploy). The evidence pack stores proposal/producer/risk/scope/verification/gate metadata and intentionally does not persist raw diffs or command output.
- Auto-merge policy integration: `autoMergeProposal` now adds a pre-mutation Gate 8 after all existing mechanical checks pass and before branch/merge mutation. It persists `~/.ashlr/evidence/<proposalId>.json`, evaluates the policy verdict, fails closed if evidence persistence fails, and refuses self-target autonomous merges unless `cfg.foundry.autoMerge.allowSelfMerge=true`.
- Agent audit cautions: do not make persisted evidence authoritative for gates because local JSON is mutable; continue recomputing risk/provenance/verification from source inputs. Future follow-up should normalize decisions ordering before claiming "latest" judge entry and can expose evidence packs in Mission Control.
- Evidence visibility pass: added bounded read/list helpers for autonomy evidence packs, `FleetStatus.autonomy`, CLI rendering, Mission Control/Fleet/Fleet Dashboard metrics, and read-only `/api/autonomy/evidence` list/detail routes. Responses remain metadata-only and omit raw diffs.
- Verification trust fix: `evaluateVerificationGate` now sorts judged decisions by timestamp and requires the newest judged decision to be `ship`; a newer `review`/non-ship verdict blocks older signed ship attestations.
- Agent next lanes: thread `workItemId`/`runId` into proposals for causal outcome records, add guard-health UX for fail-closed state/evidence blocks, and add read-only `ashlr ecosystem doctor --json --root --deep`.
- Autonomy learning foundation pass: commit `b09fde5` added proposal causal metadata (`workItemId`, `workSource`, `runId`) across daemon/swarm/best-of-N/sandboxed runs, guard-health status surfaces, read-only outcome records, and read-only ecosystem doctor.
- Next control-loop push: make worked/outcome feedback item-accurate using `proposal.workItemId`; add cheap auto-merge readiness preflight before judge calls; add bounded verify-before-judge and richer verification metadata; add a resource-aware strategy/readiness report so the fleet can choose what to build next based on budgets, guard health, model availability, and expected ROI.
- Autonomy control-loop pass: outcome feedback now records exact `workItemId` winners/empties, `merge:shipped` and judged-proposal sweeps prefer proposal causal IDs, auto-merge pass runs a cheap static readiness preflight before judge spend, verification mode verifies before judge calls with bounded `verifyBeforeJudgePerPass`, verification metadata now records detail/ran/source/time, and `ashlr fleet direction` reports resource-aware autonomous mode recommendations.

The checked-in lockfile resolves `node_modules/vite` to `6.4.3`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate` is clean, so both alerts were dismissed as inaccurate/stale dependency graph findings. Current open Dependabot alert count via `gh api` is 0.

CLI `fleet status`, `/api/fleet`, and web-control JSON now expose the current mode, confidence, resource posture, guard state, budget level, top reason, and next action.
- Idle auto-merge maintenance follow-up: daemon `tick()` now runs the gated `runAutoMergePass()` maintenance lane before returning `no-backlog` when repos are enrolled and budget/guard checks passed. Dry-runs, kill-switch, budget exhaustion, and no-enrollment paths still do not run maintenance.

Added nested package overrides for `esbuild@0.28.1` and `minimatch@10.2.5`; `npm install` in `src/raycast`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, and `npm run build` now pass. `npm run lint` remains blocked by pre-existing Raycast packaging/config issues: Raycast author `masonwyatt` returns 404 and Raycast's ESLint invocation reports all `src/**` files ignored.

When enabled, daemon ticks turn `pause` into no-dispatch, `verify-only`/`auto-merge-ready` into auto-merge maintenance without new backlog generation, `local-only` into local/builtin-constrained dispatch, and `backlog-build` into normal operation. Tick records now carry `directionMode` when the loop is active.

- Local-only routing follow-up: `local-coder` is now a first-class `EngineId` and is preserved by `foundry.autonomyControlLoop` local-only constraints, so constrained resource posture still uses the free Ollama coding backend before falling back to `builtin`.
- Direction observability follow-up: daemon ticks now persist `directionReason` and compact `autoMerge` maintenance counts (`attempted`, `judged`, `merged`). `/api/control` exposes the last applied direction mode/timestamp/reason, Mission Control shows active vs recommended direction, and Fleet Activity recent ticks carry the same metadata.
- Dispatch trace follow-up: daemon live ticks now persist bounded `dispatches` metadata per item: id/title/repo/source, final backend/tier/model, assignment path, reason, dispatched/skipped state, spend, and skip reason. The trace is metadata-only and intentionally excludes prompts, diffs, command output, and secrets.
- Dispatch trace visibility follow-up: `/api/control` emits compact dispatch log rows, `/api/fleet-activity` copies bounded dispatches onto recent ticks, and the Fleet Activity tick stream renders small backend/repo/status chips beside each tick.
- Simulation-awareness follow-up: daemon `recordTick()` now normalizes dry-run ticks with `dryRun: true`, including no-backlog, kill-switch, no-enrollment, budget, and selected-work simulation exits. `/api/control` and `/api/fleet-activity` surface that marker, and Mission Control/Fleet Activity label simulation rows without changing dispatch behavior.
- Auto-merge-ready reachability follow-up: added `listReadyEvidenceOutcomeRecords()` as a cheap daemon-facing reader that inspects bounded recent evidence packs, resolves live pending proposal state, and returns minimal outcome records without decision/judge/worked/racing joins. Daemon autonomy planning uses it only when `foundry.autoMerge.enabled=true`.
- Resource-strategy hardening follow-up: `readyEvidence` now only counts pending proposals whose latest evidence targets `main`, passes verification, is policy-allowed, and has `policy.action === "merge-main"`, preventing stale applied proposals or branch-only evidence from driving `auto-merge-ready`.
- Maintenance resource visibility follow-up: `AutoMergePassResult` now reports configured `judgePerPass` and `verifyBeforeJudgePerPass`, cap hits, verify-before-judge runs, archive/TTL drains, and a display-only `judgeEstimatedSpendUsd` based on the shared pricing helper. Daemon tick summaries, Mission Control logs, and Fleet Activity maintenance chips surface those fields.
- Agent critique decision: do not debit display-only judge estimates into daemon `todaySpentUsd` or tick `spentUsd` yet. The hard budget should use measured costs, not a made-up estimate. The next hardening pass should make `judgeProposal` return measured usage/cost and record it in the decisions ledger before using it for fail-closed maintenance budget accounting.
- Remaining autonomy risk from agent audit: auto-merge maintenance can still consume judge/verify resources without exact daemon budget charging; after measured judge usage lands, make maintenance enforce the remaining daemon budget instead of only reporting estimates.
- Daemon liveness audit: the installed `ai.ashlr.daemon` plist was stale and called `/bin/bash ~/.ashlr/bin/daemon-launch.sh`, which ran `ashlr loop --watch --allow-cloud` and exited cleanly. Reinstalling with `bin/ashlr daemon install` rewrote the plist to run `/Users/masonwyatt/.hermes/node/bin/node /Users/masonwyatt/Desktop/github/dev-tools/ashlr-hub/bin/ashlr daemon start --budget 5 --interval 1800000 --parallel 1`.
- Status truth repair: `serviceStatus()` now requires a positive launchd PID, so an installed cleanly exited job with `LastExitStatus` and no `PID` reports `running:false`. Live verification after reinstall shows launchd state `running` with daemon PID `49872`.
- Read-only status repair: `buildFleetStatus()` no longer calls `buildBacklog()`, which can run scanners, persist backlog, audit, and expand planning goals. It reads `loadBacklog()` only; live `bin/ashlr fleet status --json` now exits cleanly and reports daemon stopped/running state without goal-planner output.
- Sandbox path repair: plugin wrappers now force scanner output `repo` to the scanned root, and `buildBacklog()` coerces every scanner result to the enrolled repo being scanned. This prevents file-valued repos like `.../worktree/test/m99.backlog-actionable.test.ts` from becoming daemon cwd/worktree roots.
- Engine cwd repair: `runViaAshlrcode()` now normalizes file-valued `repoDir` inputs to their parent directory before invoking `ac` or git probes, closing the second observed `git -C .../file.ts` path.
- Auto-merge manager repair: `judgeProposal.wouldMerge` now follows configured `foundry.autoMerge.maxRisk`, `maxAutomergeFiles`, and `maxAutomergeLines`, while remaining advisory only. The real merge gate still re-checks verification, provenance, risk, scope, enrollment, policy, and kill switch.
- Guard-health repair: an armed spend guard owned by the currently running daemon PID is now treated as in-flight accounting rather than a repair-blocking stale guard. Malformed, stale, or mismatched guards still fail closed.
- Operational state after repair: `ashlr-hub` is enrolled, kill switch is off, remote is `https://github.com/ashlrai/ashlr-hub.git`, and the daemon service is installed/running under `ai.ashlr.daemon`.
- Controlled daemon upgrade note: repaired daemon runs armed spend guards while executing prior compiled code during this patch/rebuild cycle. I terminated the old PIDs, archived `daemon.spend-guard.json` and `daemon.lock` with suffixes `interrupted-upgrade-20260701-220617.bak` and `interrupted-upgrade-20260701-220821.bak`, rebuilt, reinstalled, and restarted the daemon on PID `49872` with guard health clear.
- Remaining auto-merge blockers: live status shows 2 pending proposals, 0 evidence packs, and current direction `verify-only`. The current pending proposals still need passing verification and valid frontier/judge attestations before evidence and auto-merge can occur.
- Current auto-merge/status observability pass: `FleetStatus.autoMergeReadiness` now explains pending proposal blockers without spending judge/verify resources, CLI `fleet status` renders the preflight/verify/blocked counts and top blocker reasons, and `FleetStatus.queue.next` surfaces the top persisted backlog items without refreshing scanners.
- Current guard-health pass: a spend guard owned by a live daemon PID is still accepted as in-flight only while the daemon lock heartbeat is fresh. If the lock heartbeat is stale, guard health now reports `daemon-spend-guard-stale-live-owner` so the resource strategy pauses instead of treating a wedged in-flight tick as healthy.
- Live state after the pass: stale daemon guard/lock from PID `49872` were archived, the kill switch was released with `ashlr fleet resume`, the launchd daemon was reinstalled/restarted, and `bin/ashlr daemon status --json` reports running PID `12977` with guard health clear. Fleet status reports 16 backlog items, top `queue.next` goal items, 2 pending frontier proposals, `autoMergeReadiness.knownVerificationFailed=2`, 0 evidence packs, and current direction `verify-only`.
- Executable-control critique: the previous design could compute a resource-aware `verify-only` direction while still leaving daemon enforcement advisory unless `foundry.autonomyControlLoop=true` was manually set. That made self-direction a dashboard fact instead of an operational constraint. Foundry now defaults the executable control loop on whenever a `foundry` block exists; explicit `foundry.autonomyControlLoop=false` remains available for advisory-only operation.
- Pre-scan direction critique: executable autonomy originally still called `buildBacklog()` before reading the resource strategy. That meant a `verify-only` or `pause` tick could still run scanners, plugins, and goal planning before deciding not to dispatch. Daemon ticks now use the last persisted enrolled backlog count for lightweight direction and only refresh backlog when the plan allows new dispatch.
- Stale backlog critique: live `fleet status --json` showed `queue.next` items from deleted `/var/folders/...` test repos. `FleetStatus.queue` now filters the persisted snapshot to enrolled repos that still exist, so stale fixture work no longer appears as fleet work or inflates resource-direction backlog pressure.
- Merge-gate contract critique: a legacy M86 test still expected self-target auto-merge to succeed after safety/parity checks alone. The contract now makes the current safety gate explicit: self-target autonomous merges require `foundry.autoMerge.allowSelfMerge=true`.
- Agent audit synthesis: Lorentz prioritized pre-scan resource direction, exact judge/verify budget accounting, full live config reload, resolved daemon budget defaults in strategy, conservative unknown cloud availability, local-only preselection, and separating goal planning from scanner refresh. Ampere prioritized explicit executable/advisory control-mode UX, effective config visibility, backend resource availability in fleet status, hidden-stale-backlog explanations, direction report basis labels, degraded-data diagnostics, and SSE coalescing. Boyle prioritized remote/protected unattended merge, verify/merge base binding, shared dry-run gate explanations, fail-closed baseline-red verification, optional safety checks that block on error, and broader guard-health checks for merge-critical dependencies.
- Control-mode visibility pass: added `autonomyControlMode: disabled|advisory|executable` as the explicit effective authority surface. `disabled` means no Foundry block, `advisory` means Foundry exists but `autonomyControlLoop=false`, and `executable` means daemon ticks enforce resource direction. The value is now on `FleetStatus`, `/api/fleet`, `/api/control` daemon state, CLI fleet status, and Mission Control hero/detail UI while retaining the previous boolean for compatibility.
- Full live-config reload pass: `runDaemon()` now reloads the complete config before ticks in once, continuous, and batch modes. This closes the gap where daemon tuning could refresh but Foundry policy, auto-merge settings, allowed backends, and autonomy-control mode stayed pinned to process-start config until restart.
- Backend resource status pass: `FleetStatus.backends[]` now includes `resource.availability` for every allowed backend. Sensed backends use `getResourceSnapshot()` data; allowed engines with no sensor are explicitly `not-sensed` instead of disappearing from resource awareness. CLI fleet status and `/api/fleet` expose the same field.
- Auto-merge safety audit follow-up: removed privileged GitHub merge bypass from the remote path. Ashlr now opens a PR and attempts normal host auto-merge with `gh pr merge --auto --squash`; the proposal is marked applied as a remote handoff to avoid duplicate PR creation, but `merged` remains false unless Ashlr has proof of an actual merge.
- Auto-merge explainability pass: added read-only `explainAutoMergeGate()` over the existing pure gate primitives so CLI/API/UI surfaces can tell agents and operators which static/evidence gates block auto-merge without running judges, verification, git, or inbox mutations.
- Effective config visibility pass: added a curated, no-secret effective config snapshot exposed through core API, `ashlr config effective [--json]`, and `GET /api/config/effective`, with source labels for configured/default/derived autonomy, daemon, Foundry, and backend settings.
- Merge-base binding pass: `verifyProposal()` now records the exact default branch and commit used for verification, persisted `ProposalVerifyResult` carries `baseBranch`/`baseHead`, legacy cached passing verification is re-run before trust, and auto-merge refuses staging/local/remote handoff if the default branch moved after verification.
- Fail-closed optional safety pass: when `foundry.redTeam`, `foundry.blastRadius`, or `foundry.specContract` is enabled, thrown checks, malformed results, and missing referenced specs now skip the proposal with observable `out.skipped` and `out.results` blockers instead of allowing merge by default.
- Daemon live-loop reload pass: non-once daemon loops now re-read mode, daily budget, idle backoff, and batch interval from live config each iteration and before post-tick sleep, so switching between batch/continuous behavior or interval values does not require a service restart.
- Resource unknown hardening pass: `slotsForAvailability('unknown')` is now zero slots; future unknown availability values also get zero slots. Resource-aware gateway no longer treats unknown current backends as healthy and surfaces successful demotion metadata (`demotedFrom`, `resourceState`) on final decisions.

- Current state/ambition pass agents:
  - Market/product research: current competitors emphasize background/cloud agents, PR-based collaboration, model-agnostic execution, enterprise context/governance, and AI review. Ashlr's best angle is a local-first 24/7 control plane that can choose, prove, recover, and merge across the user's own repos.
  - Architecture audit: strongest local capabilities are proposal-first daemon execution, evidence-backed auto-merge gates, live resource direction, sandbox/worktree execution, fleet status, and Mission Control visibility. Remaining gaps include exact PR merge reconciliation, stronger default confinement, config schema parity, universal verify contracts, and richer resource sensing.
  - Mission Control recovery audit: service helpers already exist (`install`, `uninstall`, `serviceStatus`); web mutations already share a token/content-type gate. Best next patch is a narrow token-gated service repair route plus read-only service health.
  - Resource audit: do not debit display-only judge estimates as real spend; instead enforce known resource availability. If Claude is cached as `throttled`, `exhausted`, or `unreachable`, judge routing should preserve Claude headroom and fall to Codex/local where available.
  - Self-improvement selection audit: self-heal writes `self-heal-queue.json` and invent appends `source:'invent'` to `backlog.json`, but a fresh backlog refresh could overwrite those generated items before selection. Best next patch is a read-only queued-autonomy scanner that rehydrates self-heal and invent work into the normal scanner set.
- Current implementation pass:
  - Added read-only `GET /api/daemon/service` and token-gated `POST /api/daemon/service/repair` using config-derived daemon service options. Mission Control now shows OS service installed/running/platform/path and exposes a Repair button when a session token is set.
  - Added `serviceStatusCached()` for Mission Control polling so `/api/control` does not synchronously probe launchd/systemd/schtasks on every refresh.
  - Added shared `daemonServiceInstallOptions()` so web recovery paths map daemon budget/interval/parallel consistently.
  - Resource-aware judge resolver now treats cached Claude `throttled` as unavailable for judge routing and falls to Codex/local instead of spending protected Claude headroom.

- Current autonomy refill/liveness/resource-sensing pass:
  - The live daemon had drained stuck proposals and entered `backlog-build`, but cached visible backlog was zero while fresh self-heal items existed in `~/.ashlr/self-heal-queue.json`. Root cause: `tick()` returned `no-backlog` before the self-heal/invent producers ran, so an empty queue could become an idle terminal state.
  - `tick()` now treats empty backlog as an active refill state: run auto-merge maintenance, run self-heal, rebuild backlog, and only if still empty run bounded generative invent and rebuild again. If self-heal creates concrete work, invention is skipped for that tick. Producer maintenance now runs before the spend guard so an armed guard covers actual selected dispatches, not discovery work.
  - `runDaemon()` now keeps the singleton lock heartbeat fresh every 30s for the full process lifetime. Guard health now requires a matching fresh daemon lock heartbeat for an armed spend guard owned by a live pid; missing/stale heartbeats become a `daemon-spend-guard-stale-live-owner` blocker.
  - Service install/repair now uses the shared `daemonServiceInstallOptions()` defaulting to the effective daemon cadence (`intervalMs=300000`) instead of the older service generator fallback (`1800000`), keeping OS service restarts aligned with the runtime loop.
  - Claude CLI `rate_limit_event` lines are captured from `claude` stdout/stderr, sanitized into `~/.ashlr/fabric/claude-rate-limit-events.jsonl`, and read by ResourceMonitor before OAuth/transcript fallback. Fresh high-pressure `seven_day`/`five_hour` events constrain Claude automatically; expired events and low-utilization metadata are ignored.

- Current live watchdog hardening:
  - Live restart smoke on the new refill loop revealed daemon-launched `npm run test` can leave Vitest worker grandchildren alive after the direct npm process exits or is interrupted. That can stall a 24/7 daemon tick even though `runVerifyCommand()` had a `spawnSync` timeout.

The yield nudge runs after poor-prior and high-cost de-escalation so it cannot preempt safer budget/risk reductions.

- Current global workspace / agent-action telemetry pass:
  - Research anchors: Anthropic's `Global workspace in Claude` post and linked transformer-circuits paper argue for a small, reportable, controllable, flexible, selective internal workspace (J-space/J-lens) as an observability and safety substrate; the released `anthropics/jacobian-lens` repo makes the probe work reproducible for open-weight experiments, but production Ashlr should treat hidden-state probes as advisory only. Adjacent work on entropy-based observability, blackboard multi-agent systems, code-as-agent-harness, and learning retrieval from agent trajectories reinforces the same product direction: trace everything important, broadcast bounded shared state, and learn from trajectories.
  - Implementation direction from the agents: build a software-level Ashlr Global Workspace now, not a model-hidden-state dependency. It should be append-only, metadata-only by default, secret-scrubbed, bounded, typed, readable by agents, visible to operators, and wired into daemon decisions, dispatch outcomes, verification, judge/merge, and future reflection checkpoints.
  - Added `src/core/fleet/agent-action-ledger.ts`, an append-only `agent-actions/YYYY-MM-DD.jsonl` stream under `$ASHLR_HOME` (or `~/.ashlr` fallback). It records compact `AgentActionEvent` rows, reads newest-first with window/file caps, skips malformed lines, normalizes invalid timestamps, omits non-finite numeric fields, scrubs text/counts/tags, and rebuilds legacy rows field-by-field so poisoned enum-like dimensions cannot become workspace topics.
  - Daemon `tick()` now records durable agent actions for no-op/guard/dry-run/dispatch paths and mirrors dispatch-production rows into agent-action events. Dispatch events preserve machine, item, repo, source, backend/tier/model, proposal/run ids, outcome, spend, and compact counts without raw prompts, diffs, tool args, or stdout.
  - `readAgentWorkspace()` produces a bounded global-workspace status with event count, latest timestamp, active machines, spend, proposal/no-proposal counts, top action/outcome/repo/backend buckets, simple entropy signals, attention topics, and recent actions.
  - Surfaces now expose that status through `FleetStatus.workspace`, `ashlr fleet status`, `fleet watch`, Mission Control, Fleet view, Fleet Dashboard production panel, `/api/fleet-state`, and Fleet Activity's `recentActions` feed. Empty installs stay quiet; partial stale status objects degrade safely.

  - Added `PhantomCapabilitySnapshot` to `PhantomStatus`. It reports `valueMode:"metadata-and-names-only"`, safe secret-name counts, known fleet secret present/missing counts, Pulse PAT/token credential booleans, metadata status, child env injection availability, MCP availability, and mutation approval posture. Secret values are never read or returned.
  - Hardened `src/core/phantom.ts`: known fleet names now include both `ASHLR_PULSE_PAT` and `ASHLR_PULSE_TOKEN`; JSON object fields, flat string arrays, and plain-text fallback output all run through a strict uppercase env-name allowlist; token families such as `github_pat_`, `glpat-`, `hf_`, `npm_`, `AIza`, `sk-`, `ghp_`, Slack tokens, AWS access keys, JWTs, and long value-shaped strings cannot masquerade as names.
  - Structured `phantom status --json` now fails closed for unknown arrays/objects and treats structured `error`/`message` strings containing "not initialized" or "run phantom init" as uninitialized. This avoids reporting injection readiness from ambiguous or error-shaped JSON.
  - Readiness/preflight now includes a reduced Phantom object with counts/booleans only. MCP source paths are normalized to `~/.ashlr/...` before display; the focused test asserts readiness JSON does not contain concrete secret identifiers such as `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` or `ASHLR_PULSE_PAT`.
  - FleetStatus now exposes an optional cached `phantom` block populated through `getCachedFleetPhantomStatus()` with a 30s cache and 500ms per-command timeout for dashboard-safe polling. Dashboard/control inherit the field through existing `fleet` snapshots; no new dashboard child-process probe was added.
  - CLI `ashlr fleet status` renders a compact line such as `Phantom: not-initialized v0.6.0, 0/6 known fleet secrets, pulse no, nim no, mcp yes, injection disabled, values hidden`.
  - Live smoke on this machine: `bin/ashlr preflight --json` reports Phantom installed `0.6.0`, initialized false, MCP configured from `~/.ashlr/settings.json`; `bin/ashlr fleet status --json` reports `state:"not-initialized"`, 0/6 known fleet secrets, MCP configured, and values hidden. - Current hub secret-safety invariant plane:
  - Parallel agent audits agreed on the next compounding risk: Ashlr is intentionally collecting more agent trajectory data, so the metadata ledgers need a single strong fake-secret canary before the learning loop expands. Highest-risk gaps were decisions `reason`, direct genome hub appends, dispatch-production field passthrough, raw MCP/public views, and proposal/dashboard read surfaces.

It now catches PEM/private-key blocks, `github_pat_`, GitLab `glpat-`, HuggingFace `hf_`, npm `npm_`, Google `AIza...`, URL authority passwords, connection strings, access/refresh/session/id tokens, `_authToken`, long base64 blobs, and the existing `sk-`, GitHub short-prefix, bearer, Slack, AWS, JWT, and hex-64 patterns.

Decisions scrub `reason`, `verdict`, `engine`, `model`, `proposalId`, `workItemId`, `runId`, and `detail` before `normalizeDecisionLearningFields()` and append.
  - Dispatch-production no longer returns/writes `...event` plus a few scrubbed overrides. It builds an explicit sanitized event with scrubbed machine/item/source/repo/title/backend/tier/model/assignedBy/route/outcome/proposal/run/trajectory/reason/basis fields and non-negative numeric guards before append and on legacy readback.
  - `appendHubEntry()` now scrubs direct genome hub title/text/project/tags before append, and `loadHubEntries()` scrubs legacy hub JSONL rows before normal `loadGenome()`/export/API consumers see them. Auto-capture was already scrubbed, but direct learn/store paths are now protected too.

- Current Best-of-N file-once proposal-capture pass:
  - Added `draftOnly` to `captureSandboxedProposal()`. Draft capture reads the live sandbox diff, runs the same triviality/completeness gate, scrubs secrets, computes `diffHash`, signs provenance, and returns a proposal-shaped draft without persisting an inbox proposal or writing a `proposed` decision-ledger row.
  - `runBestOfN()` now owns one sandbox per candidate when the full sandbox/capture helpers are available. Candidate runs use `propose:false`, retain the worktree, draft-capture proposal material for judging/taste scoring, then final-capture only the selected ranked winner before returning. Cleanup removes all candidate sandboxes in `finally`.

That keeps dispatch-production yield truthful while preserving race telemetry.

Losers are no longer persisted as pending-then-rejected proposals, so they no longer pollute inbox quality metrics, anti-clog cooldowns, proposal counts, or decision-ledger ROI. The Best-of-N ledger still records every candidate; loser rows use `proposalId:null` and `won:false`.

Malformed/non-hex attestation strings still pass through the scrubber. Full CI caught this because generic long-hex scrubbing had turned a valid attestation into `[REDACTED]`, causing the verification gate to report an HMAC mismatch before the stale-base merge guard.

- Current daemon capture-missing learning pass:

- Current delete-only evidence pack pass:
  - Scout finding: `summarizeDiff()` only collected paths from `+++` lines, so delete-only diffs with `+++ /dev/null` could produce evidence packs with `diff.files: []` even though the proposal removed a real file. That made the durable evidence misleading and could cause policy to reject real delete-only changes as empty/unparsable.
  - Implementation: diff evidence now collects changed paths from `diff --git`, `---`, `+++`, `rename from`, and `rename to` headers through a `Set`, skips `/dev/null`, and still stores only metadata (`files`, `changedLines`, optional hash) rather than raw diff text or deleted content.
  - Regression coverage: `m301` now builds a delete-only diff, asserts `pack.diff.files === ['docs/obsolete.md']`, `changedLines === 1`, policy allows the otherwise-good pack, and persisted JSON excludes both `diff --git` and deleted content.
  - Verification passed: `npm run test:ci -- test/m301.autonomy-policy.test.ts` (16 tests), `npm run typecheck -- --pretty false`, `npm run lint` (known 115-warning baseline, 0 errors), `npm run build`, `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`, and `git diff --check`.

- Current executable diagnostic reslice drain pass:
  - Scout finding: `drain-diagnostic-reslices` was a Fleet OS recommendation but still invoked generic `ashlr daemon start --once`; live evidence showed the daemon verifying generic work while all five `proposal-repair-nodiff` items stayed queued. The action could neither guarantee nor prove the reslice lane was draining.
  - Implementation: daemon start now accepts `--drain diagnostic-reslices`, threaded through `runDaemon()` and `tick()`. In that mode, selection filters to trusted diagnostic no-diff reslice items before normal repo round-robin, while preserving existing coordinator claims, cooldowns, pending-proposal dedupe, budget caps, dry-run release, sandboxed proposal dispatch, and proposal-only authority.
  - Provenance selector: the daemon reuses the exported `isTrustedDiagnosticResliceItem()` predicate, requiring the hashed `:proposal-repair-nodiff:` id shape, `proposal-repair` / `diagnostic-reslice` / `dispatch-no-diff-reslice` tags, and diagnostic detail text. This avoids accepting arbitrary no-diff prose.
  - Telemetry: targeted ticks now carry `drain:{mode,available,selected,selectedItemIds?,stalled?}`. Tick-start and a pre-dispatch `daemon:drain-select` agent action persist bounded selected ids and counts only. No prompts, diffs, stdout/stderr, env, file contents, or command output are added.

- Current verified-skill trust-boundary hardening pass:
  - Adversarial result: production shadow retrieval was stopped before wiring because append-only card rows were not yet a canonical authority boundary. The audit identified forgeable source/status claims, absent lifecycle revocation, caller-controlled legacy skill privilege, permissive ledger modes, future-date crowding, and unsigned duplicate revisions.
  - Provenance and attestation: `learnFromApplied()` now requires the authoritative proposal HMAC before writing either legacy or structured learning. Structured cards use controlled retrieval text only, carry a canonical SHA-256 content hash, and receive a domain-separated host-local HMAC binding content hash, skill id, revision, proposal id, and verified diff hash. Retrieval rejects missing, tampered, stale, chained, manual/imported, or otherwise incomplete card revisions.
  - Canonical lifecycle: candidate ranking is deterministic, latest-revision-wins, conflict-quarantining, and capped at two, but remains unwired and injects zero context. Real-world revert detection appends a newly signed `revoked` revision; follow-up fixes append `deprecated`; revoked is terminal and unsigned cards cannot be converted into trusted lifecycle state.
  - Local safety: skill directories/files are enforced at `0700`/`0600` on POSIX, unsafe owners/symlinks are refused, future-dated rows/files are bounded, malformed batch siblings remain isolated, and canonical digests bypass generic secret heuristics without accepting arbitrary text.

- Current durable attempt identity pass:
  - Parallel audit result: daemon dispatch had no identity allocated before execution, Best-of-N loser identities were not externally visible or durable, concurrent manifests could not join intent to execution, and caller-supplied sandbox run ids reached filenames without a shared bounded validator.
  - Identity primitive: added opaque UUIDv4 outer attempt ids and domain-separated deterministic candidate ids. Both formats are path-safe, contain no repo/work/prompt text, add no Best-of-N fanout ceiling, and reject malformed parents, ordinals, path-like ids, control characters, and oversized execution ids.
  - Propagation: daemon-selected work now receives one attempt id before task execution. The same id reaches delegation scope, builtin swarm, ordinary `runGoal`, API/CLI sandbox execution, TITRR retries, error/no-proposal traces, dispatch-production events, and agent-action outcomes. Best-of-N retains the outer trajectory while each candidate gets a stable child run id.
  - Durable joins: concurrent dispatch manifests now record assignment attempt ids before execution. Best-of-N results and append-only candidate rows now retain the outer attempt id plus every winner/loser candidate run id, including missing-runner and failure outcomes.
  - Safety boundary: this pass changes no backend, tier, model, route choice, prompt/goal text, budget, retry count, winner selection, proposal content, verification, merge authority, or skill context. Production still does not read/select skill cards or write skill-use events.
  - Independent review fixes: fresh caller-supplied run/swarm id collisions now fail closed without overwriting persisted state; `resumeId` explicitly discards `runId`; invalid Best-of-N identities become candidate errors; invalid swarm ids return failed `SwarmRun`s instead of throwing; same-id TITRR invocations append durable log sections instead of overwriting earlier evidence; and every preallocated terminal skip trace retains its manifest identity.
  - Remaining boundary: serial dispatch still lacks a pre-executor append-only start row, and builtin swarm proposal outcomes remain less precisely typed than sandboxed-engine outcomes. Shadow use production stays disabled until those semantics and candidate-accurate selection are proven.

- Current crash-visible start and builtin outcome truth pass:
  - Attempt lifecycle: the daemon now appends one metadata-only `daemon:dispatch-start` action immediately before each real builtin, single-run, or outer Best-of-N executor invocation. Preflight, dry-run, budget, autonomy-pause, kill, throttle, resource, and unassigned skips emit no false start. The start uses the preallocated outer attempt/trajectory identity and contains no work title, goal, prompt, diff, output, environment, command, or file content.
  - Builtin production truth: `SwarmRun` now carries an orthogonal `proposalOutcome` beside execution `status`. Sandbox capture classifies filed, empty, completeness-blocked, capture-error, disabled, sandbox-unavailable, and failed-no-diff outcomes; proposal ids and bounded diff counts flow directly into daemon dispatch-production telemetry instead of being inferred from pending-count deltas.
  - Cleanup and durability: completeness-gate rejection no longer returns before worktree cleanup. Capture outcomes persist after the final sandbox diff, mandatory-sandbox and governance failures persist under their preallocated attempt ids, and sandboxed dry-run planning failures still leave no swarm record. - Current terminal generated-repair lifecycle pass:
  - Live trigger: generated capture and diagnostic repairs remained pending after successful or repeatedly empty attempts, so the daemon could spend scarce editing slots on terminal work indefinitely.
  - Authority model: the first analytics-ledger classifier design was rejected during adversarial review because coarse `worked` and unsigned outcome rows could suppress valid work. The implemented lifecycle retires only from an exact durable, complete, `done`, nonempty proposal bound to the repair item, canonical repo, run, trajectory, and generation; it exhausts only after two distinct explicit empty-diff attempts. Aggregate Best-of-N outcomes, failed or partial captures, infrastructure failures, stale proposals, mismatched identities, and caller-shaped records grant no terminal authority.
  - Durable state: local mode stores a versioned, metadata-only lifecycle under `~/.ashlr/fleet/generated-repair-lifecycle.json`. Generation and attempt identities are SHA-256 digests; raw goals, prompts, diffs, output, environment, commands, repo paths, and item text are absent. Timestamp recurrence creates a new generation while presentation-only changes do not.
  - Failure boundary: writes use token-owned exclusive locking, atomic replacement, owner-only modes, and a durable failure marker. Lock contention, corruption, impossible state, duplicate generations, or write failure make lifecycle unavailable and block generated-repair dispatch until a successful authoritative write or operator repair clears the condition. Shared mode neither reads nor writes local lifecycle state and blocks local proposal-repair dispatch.
  - Queue truth: terminal work is removed from both the mutable self-heal queue and autonomy backlog before selection. Strict queue reads preserve malformed bytes, prune counts advance only after persistence succeeds, ordinary work is untouched, and an active newer generation supersedes an older terminal key in the same tick.
  - Crash recovery: exact persisted proposals are reconciled into lifecycle before dispatch, preventing a daemon crash between proposal filing and lifecycle write from re-running completed repair work.
  - Process recovery: proposal-producing swarms persist the work item, generation hash, source, and bounded sandbox/proposal resume flags on `SwarmRun`. Detached workers and CLI resumes restore the persisted contract before sandbox setup and cannot replace its causal identity or downgrade a mandatory sandbox with fresh flags.
  - Next lane: preserve and gate partial TITRR producer diffs before failed producer sandbox cleanup. Keep that capture change separate from terminal lifecycle authority so partial output cannot accidentally become terminal evidence.

- Current metadata-only external-agent diagnostics pass:
  - Privacy boundary: future external-agent diagnostics persist a fixed schema containing only a domain-hashed run reference, fixed engine/outcome/error labels, bounded counters, and output/error byte-line-presence shapes. Raw run ids, goals, prompts, command argv, paths, diffs, stdout/stderr, environment, file contents, and exception text never cross the persistence API.
  - Retry truth: `runEngineSandboxed()` records one row immediately after every real executor invocation, including failed retries and compatibility recovery counts. Repeated top-level invocations append instead of overwriting evidence, and Best-of-N/dispatch semantics remain unchanged.
  - Filesystem boundary: diagnostics use owner-only directories/files, no-follow opens, owner/inode checks, hashed filenames, malformed-tail refusal, per-run 64 KiB limits, 30-day/2,000-file/64 MiB retention, and fail-closed behavior for unsafe entries. Windows persistence is disabled until an equivalent private-store contract exists.
  - Concurrency: a bounded global append lock serializes maintenance and writes across processes; per-run locks preserve append integrity. A real 16-process regression burst persists all 16 rows instead of silently dropping concurrent fleet completions.
  - Crash/clock safety: lock owners require PID plus process-start identity, cached mismatches require uncached confirmation, and malformed owners use monotonic inode-bound observation grace. Dead, reused-PID, malformed, future-dated, and replacement-generation cases recover without letting wall-clock changes evict a verified live owner. Standalone maintenance participates in the same append-to-maintenance lock order as writers and revalidates lock generations before retention.
  - Legacy policy: existing raw `.log` bytes remain operator-owned and are never parsed, rewritten, migrated, or removed by this rollout. Store hardening changes only their enclosing directory to `0700` and file modes to `0600`.

- Current objective-bound repair-authority pass:
  - Live evidence: the current queue and journal contain no evidence capable of proving a general `no-change-required` outcome. The attempted synchronous shadow verifier was removed before release because scanner absence is not source-specific proof and repo verification on the daemon path could delay durable handoff, production, and state persistence.
  - Objective identity: daemon production records now carry a fixed 64-character objective fingerprint over canonical repo, item id, source, scrubbed title, and scrubbed detail. The fingerprint uses NFC/whitespace normalization plus a host-local HMAC and is minted only when the existing provenance key is durably present as the expected 32-byte private key; ephemeral or truncated keys fail closed.
  - Repair authority: no-diff handoffs and queue projections accept only validated lowercase fingerprints. Diagnostic generations require exact handoff id, generation, child, repo, parent id, source, backend, tier, and objective fingerprint. A scanner reusing a stable id with changed acceptance criteria is quarantined rather than silently inheriting old lifecycle or cooldown state.
  - Replay and compaction: missing-versus-present or changed objective fingerprints are conflicts in either row order. Hash-bearing observations require complete routing provenance. Compaction preserves every semantic event fingerprint and removes only physical replay/invalid rows, so a late replay cannot mint authority after an older generation was compacted away.
  - Migration: pre-fingerprint diagnostic queue rows cannot use fallback lifecycle generations and are deterministically removed from both mutable queue projections. The count remains visible as `dispatchRepairPruned`; ordinary generated proposal/capture repairs retain their prior fallback lifecycle behavior.
  - Capacity/privacy: malformed runtime values are omitted before journal or queue persistence. The 100,000-row marker remains an explicit health signal but no longer empties parsed authority or blocks compaction; the 256 MiB file cap remains the hard bound. Supplied maintenance events do not create journal authority.

- Current bounded advisory resolution-observer pass:
  - Observation authority: every merge-contract `present` or `absent` row now carries a host-keyed HMAC over its canonical repo, scanner contract, status, chronology, objective identity, and authenticated source-base digest. Backlog persistence remains backward-compatible, but unsigned legacy rows cannot seed or resolve observer state. Source-base and observation comparisons are constant-time.
  - Durable correlation: each full backlog generation has a random snapshot id. Resident ticks persist the exact generation/id pair, the parent validates that pair once, and the child receives and revalidates both before any checkpoint or witness mutation. Stale, replaced, partial, degraded, truncated, over-cap, non-monotonic, or unattested snapshots fail closed.
  - Process containment: observer work runs in a no-stdio child with a 250 ms aggregate advisory deadline and a 500 ms parent kill boundary. Completion normally waits for OS `close`; shutdown cancels and awaits before daemon lock release. Kill-confirmation fallback is bounded, releases process-local single-flight state, and cross-process execution locking prevents overlapping cursor mutation.
  - Replay and persistence: transition identity derives from canonical pre/post evidence rather than mutable backlog or observation timestamps. Fresh re-observations replay one signed physical witness after checkpoint failure. Cursor writes use monotonic compare-and-set semantics, readers rebind the pathname to the opened inode after every read, and the latest run is stored separately so failed attempts cannot hide behind an older successful cursor.
  - Cryptographic/storage hardening: witness rows are HMAC-attested with the protected provenance key; unsigned or altered rows degrade the ledger. Provenance key load/create rejects unsafe ancestors, links, ownership/mode/length violations, and replacement races, while safely recovering the unique temporary hardlink left by a crashed atomic installer.
  - Operational truth: Fleet Status and CLI expose observer source health, cursor/run/witness state, pending objectives, witness count, outcome, lag, and freshness. `source-unavailable`, stale, cancelled, deadline, capacity, and write failures lead with degraded health. The observer remains advisory only, with no proposal, lifecycle, dispatch, verification, learning-label, or merge consumer.

- Current autonomous metadata context-rollup pass:
  - Semantic boundary: autonomous context rollups are a new `context-rollup` action kind, not reflection. They remain count-only observations and therefore cannot clear `reflection-missing`, suppress `proposal-yield-low`, or alter genome memory, prompts, routing, proposals, verification, merge, or deployment authority.
  - Evidence contract: only exact `daemon:dispatch` terminal events with authoritative learning labels, `daemon-dispatch` provenance, and matching `runId`, `run:<runId>`, and run-summary identity contribute. Events are deduplicated by trajectory inside the configured cadence window; selection, maintenance, reflection, malformed, derived-work, and unauthoritative rows contribute nothing.
  - Cadence/idempotency: default policy is enabled, 24 hours, and 50 unique terminal trajectories, with floors/caps of 1..168 hours and 25..5,000 trajectories. A new rollup requires both cadence expiry and a source event newer than the prior source watermark. A deterministic SHA-256 metadata identity over policy, watermark, and fixed counts collapses concurrent physical duplicates into one workspace signal.
  - Persistence/privacy: cadence reads are fixed-key filtered, bounded to 5,001 matches, and require complete parseable files. Unreadable, malformed, truncated, or failed synced appends emit nothing. The persisted row has a static summary, fixed tags, policy/version/watermark, and numeric counts only; no repo, item, run, model, prompt, summary, reason, diff, output, environment, route, or source text is copied.
  - Scheduling: resident and one-shot live daemons invoke the rollup only after an `ok` tick and persisted daemon state. Dry-run, disabled, non-ok, low-signal, stale-evidence, cadence-active, and unavailable paths are explicit no-ops.
  - Verification: focused configuration, privacy, cadence, restart, dedup, writer, status, and daemon suites passed `232/232`; build, typecheck, high-severity audit, diff checks, and lint (known warning baseline only) passed. The first full suite exposed one clock-bound M349 privacy fixture just beyond 48 hours; its invariant window is now stable at seven days.
